# IMPORTANT: Source Code Access

**Local source files are not present.** Your workspace does not contain source code. You **MUST** use Sourcegraph MCP tools to discover, read, and understand code before making any changes.

Use `sg_list_repos` to discover available repositories before searching.


## Required Workflow

1. **Search first** — Use MCP tools to find relevant files and understand existing patterns
2. **Read remotely** — Use `sg_read_file` to read full file contents from Sourcegraph
3. **Edit locally** — Use Edit, Write, and Bash to create or modify files in your working directory
4. **Verify locally** — Run tests with Bash to check your changes

## Tool Selection

| Goal | Tool |
|------|------|
| Exact symbol/string | `sg_keyword_search` |
| Concepts/semantic search | `sg_nls_search` |
| Trace usage/callers | `sg_find_references` |
| See implementation | `sg_go_to_definition` |
| Read full file | `sg_read_file` |
| Browse structure | `sg_list_files` |
| Find repos | `sg_list_repos` |
| Search commits | `sg_commit_search` |
| Track changes | `sg_diff_search` |
| Compare versions | `sg_compare_revisions` |

**Decision logic:**
1. Know the exact symbol? → `sg_keyword_search`
2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`
3. Need definition of a symbol? → `sg_go_to_definition`
4. Need all callers/references? → `sg_find_references`
5. Need full file content? → `sg_read_file`

## Scoping (Always Do This)

```
repo:^github.com/ORG/REPO$           # Exact repo (preferred)
repo:github.com/ORG/                 # All repos in org
file:.*\.ts$                         # TypeScript only
file:src/api/                        # Specific directory
```

Start narrow. Expand only if results are empty.

## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

## If Stuck

If MCP search returns no results:
1. Broaden the search query (synonyms, partial identifiers)
2. Try `sg_nls_search` for semantic matching
3. Use `sg_list_files` to browse the directory structure
4. Use `sg_list_repos` to verify the repository name

45-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've completed a comprehensive analysis of rate limiting middleware patterns across Envoy and Kubernetes. Here's a summary of what I found:

## Key Findings

**Envoy Rate Limiting Implementation:**
- **Local Rate Limiting** - Three layers: HTTP filters, network filters, and a common implementation using token buckets
- **Global Rate Limiting** - Uses gRPC-based service (RLQS) with GlobalRateLimitClientImpl for streaming quota updates and LocalRateLimitClientImpl for thread-safe worker access
- Core pattern: Token bucket with support for dynamic descriptor-based buckets and distributed sharing

**Kubernetes Rate Limiting Implementation:**
- **Token Bucket** - Wraps golang.org/x/time/rate.Limiter with configurable QPS and burst
- **API Priority and Fairness (APF)** - Multi-layered system:
  - apf_filter.go: Interface defining Handle/Run/Install methods
  - apf_controller.go: Manages PriorityLevelConfiguration objects and state
  - priority-and-fairness.go: HTTP middleware for request classification and queueing
  - Bootstrap configs with mandatory and suggested priority levels

Both systems implement rate limiting with token buckets, but Kubernetes APF adds sophisticated priority-based queue management and fair queueing for adaptive concurrency control at the API server level.

I've created `/workspace/answer.json` with:
- 22 relevant source files
- 36 key symbols (classes, functions, interfaces)
- 12 call chains showing data flow
- Detailed narrative explanation of both architectures

The implementation spans multiple layers in each project.\\n\\n## Envoy Rate Limiting Architecture\\n\\n**Local Rate Limiting** is implemented across multiple components:\\n\\n1. **HTTP Local Rate Limit Filter** (source/extensions/filters/http/local_ratelimit/): The Filter class implements Http::PassThroughFilter and intercepts requests. It uses FilterConfig to manage the rate limiter instance and calls decodeHeaders() to check if requests should be rate limited. The config holds LocalRateLimiterImpl which implements the actual token bucket logic.\\n\\n2. **Network Local Rate Limit Filter** (source/extensions/filters/network/local_ratelimit/): The Filter class implements Network::ReadFilter and enforces rate limiting at the connection level via onNewConnection().
